# RPCE Practice Questions (generated, RONR 12th-ed.-grounded)

1000 questions across 506 concepts, generated from the transcribed *Robert's Rules of Order Newly Revised, 12th ed.* corpus. Every answer cites the exact section and quotes it verbatim (spec §7). Question types are varied (cloze recall, quote→section, stated-in-section), following [`RPCE-Sample-Questions-v4-100625.md`](./RPCE-Sample-Questions-v4-100625.md).

**Spaced-repetition grouping.** Each item is tagged `[Concept Cxxxx · format]`. Items that share a **Concept ID** are the *same concept in different formats*: the app schedules them as **one problem on a single FSRS schedule** and *rotates* the format each repetition — never the same shape twice in a row (spec §7.1 / SPOV 1, the Transfer Ladder). The format tag is how the scheduler tracks answers of the same type.

> Reproduce with `python pylib/tools/rpce_generate_questions.py`.

3. `[C0139 · cloze]` Answer: **Resolved**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-15) — "If the resolution is offered in a mass meeting (or in any meeting where there is no established organization whose act the adopted resolution would become), it may begin, “Resolved, That it is the sense of this meeting that…” A resolution can consist of more than one resolving clause, as in the following example:"
4. `[C0139 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-15) — "If the resolution is offered in a mass meeting (or in any meeting where there is no established organization whose act the adopted resolution would become), it may begin, “Resolved, That it is the sense of this meeting that…” A resolution can consist of more than one resolving clause, as in the following example:"
5. `[C0194 · cloze]` Answer: **Subsidiary motions**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-3) — "Subsidiary motions assist the assembly in treating or disposing of a main motion (and sometimes other motions)."
6. `[C0194 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-3) — "Subsidiary motions assist the assembly in treating or disposing of a main motion (and sometimes other motions)."
7. `[C0196 · cloze]` Answer: **agree to**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:52](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-52) — "A motion to adopt (or accept or agree to) an officer’s or a committee’s report or recommendations which the assembly (by means of a main motion) directed the officer or committee to prepare is an incidental main motion."
8. `[C0196 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:52](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-52) — "A motion to adopt (or accept or agree to) an officer’s or a committee’s report or recommendations which the assembly (by means of a main motion) directed the officer or committee to prepare is an incidental main motion."
9. `[C0238 · cloze]` Answer: **Amend**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-11) — "All of them take precedence over motions of any other class (except in certain instances where the immediately pending question may be a motion to Amend, a motion for the Previous Question, or an incidental motion that was moved while a still higher-ranking privileged motion was immediately pending)."
10. `[C0238 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-11) — "All of them take precedence over motions of any other class (except in certain instances where the immediately pending question may be a motion to Amend, a motion for the Previous Question, or an incidental motion that was moved while a still higher-ranking privileged motion was immediately pending)."
11. `[C0329 · cloze]` Answer: **after**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-4) — "In the case of the subsidiary motions only, their distinguishing characteristics as a class are explained after this description of the individual motions, since these characteristics will be more easily understood if the material is read in that order."
12. `[C0329 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [6:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-6-4) — "In the case of the subsidiary motions only, their distinguishing characteristics as a class are explained after this description of the individual motions, since these characteristics will be more easily understood if the material is read in that order."
13. `[C0369 · cloze]` Answer: **refrain**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-11) — "A motion whose only effect is to propose that the assembly refrain from doing something should not be offered if the same result can be accomplished by offering no motion at all."
14. `[C0369 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-11) — "A motion whose only effect is to propose that the assembly refrain from doing something should not be offered if the same result can be accomplished by offering no motion at all."
15. `[C0380 · cloze]` Answer: **Division of a Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [10:25](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-25) — "In the case of a series of resolutions relating to a single subject, if members desire one or more of the resolutions to be considered separately, the motion for Division of a Question (27) must be made and adopted by a majority vote."

[10:25](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-10-25) — "In the case of a series of resolutions relating to a single subject, if members desire one or more of the resolutions to be considered separately, the motion for Division of a Question (27) must be made and adopted by a majority vote."

## Domain 2: Subsidiary and Privileged Motions

**1.** `[C0016 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: Rules limiting the time to which a question can be postponed are related to the terms meeting and _____ (8), as follows:

**2.** `[C0016 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: Rules limiting the time to which a question can be postponed are related to the terms _____ and session (8), as follows:

   A. meeting
   B. exhausted his right to debate
   C. in good standing
   D. extending limits

**3.** `[C0020 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: Assume that the following resolution is pending in a meeting of a local unit of a state professional society: “_____, That the Ferndale Unit endorse the State President of the Society, James Thornton, for the office of United States Senator.” Debate creates a delicate situation.

**4.** `[C0020 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: Assume that the following resolution is pending in a meeting of a local unit of a state professional society: “_____, That the Ferndale Unit endorse the State President of the Society, James Thornton, for the office of United States Senator.” Debate creates a delicate situation.

   A. presents
   B. cumulative voting
   C. executive director,
   D. Resolved

**5.** `[C0023 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: Since a motion to _____ may be voted down because a majority wish to hear one speech or take one vote, this motion must be renewable as soon as there has been any progress in business or even material progress in debate.

**6.** `[C0023 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: If a member who has not properly obtained the floor calls out, “I move to adjourn,” such a call cannot be entertained as a motion except by unanimous consent (see _____, 39).

   B. Dilatory Motions
   C. rank
   D. interrupted

**225.** `[C1159 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: A motion to _____ by striking out an entire paragraph, section, or article—or a complete main motion or resolution—and inserting a different paragraph or other unit in its place is called a motion to substitute, and the paragraph or resolution to be inserted is said to be offered (or proposed) as “a substitute.” A substitute can be offered for a paragraph or a main motion of only one sentence, and in such a case the paragraph proposed as a substitute can contain several sentences.

**Answer Key** (with Concept ID · format for SRS tracking)

1. `[C0016 · cloze]` Answer: **session**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-5) — "Rules limiting the time to which a question can be postponed are related to the terms meeting and session (8), as follows:"
2. `[C0016 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-5) — "Rules limiting the time to which a question can be postponed are related to the terms meeting and session (8), as follows:"
3. `[C0020 · cloze]` Answer: **Resolved**. See RONR (12th ed.) [11:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-11-6) — "Assume that the following resolution is pending in a meeting of a local unit of a state professional society: “Resolved, That the Ferndale Unit endorse the State President of the Society, James Thornton, for the office of United States Senator.” Debate creates a delicate situation."
4. `[C0020 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [11:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-11-6) — "Assume that the following resolution is pending in a meeting of a local unit of a state professional society: “Resolved, That the Ferndale Unit endorse the State President of the Society, James Thornton, for the office of United States Senator.” Debate creates a delicate situation."
5. `[C0023 · cloze]` Answer: **Adjourn**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-13) — "Since a motion to Adjourn may be voted down because a majority wish to hear one speech or take one vote, this motion must be renewable as soon as there has been any progress in business or even material progress in debate."
6. `[C0023 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-13) — "If a member who has not properly obtained the floor calls out, “I move to adjourn,” such a call cannot be entertained as a motion except by unanimous consent (see Dilatory Motions, 39)."
7. `[C0057 · cloze]` Answer: **to a Certain Time**. See RONR (12th ed.) [15:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-15-11) — "After the adoption of an order that does provide a time for closing debate on the main question—either at a specified hour or after debate for a specified length of time, as in Form and Example (b) or (f) below—motions to Commit or to Postpone to a Certain Time are not in order, since providing a time for closing debate implies that at that time the question will be voted on."
8. `[C0057 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [15:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-15-11) — "After the adoption of an order that does provide a time for closing debate on the main question—either at a specified hour or after debate for a specified length of time, as in Form and Example (b) or (f) below—motions to Commit or to Postpone to a Certain Time are not in order, since providing a time for closing debate implies that at that time the question will be voted on."
9. `[C0059 · cloze]` Answer: **Reconsider**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-17) — "Reconsideration of a Vote While the Previous Question Is in Effect."
10. `[C0059 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-17) — "Reconsideration of a Vote While the Previous Question Is in Effect."
11. `[C0062 · cloze]` Answer: **Commit**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:2](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-2) — "The motion to Commit also has three variations whose object is not to turn the main question over to a smaller group, but to permit the assembly’s full meeting body to consider it with the greater freedom of debate that is allowed in committees—that is, with no limit on the number of times a member can speak."
12. `[C0062 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:2](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-2) — "The motion to Commit also has three variations whose object is not to turn the main question over to a smaller group, but to permit the assembly’s full meeting body to consider it with the greater freedom of debate that is allowed in committees—that is, with no limit on the number of times a member can speak."
13. `[C0070 · cloze]` Answer: **Previous Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-12) — "If debate has been closed by ordering the Previous Question or by the expiration of the time to which debate was limited, then up until the moment of taking the last vote under the order, the questions still before the assembly can be laid on the table."
14. `[C0070 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [17:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-17-12) — "If debate has been closed by ordering the Previous Question or by the expiration of the time to which debate was limited, then up until the moment of taking the last vote under the order, the questions still before the assembly can be laid on the table."
15. `[C0073 · cloze]` Answer: **Previous Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:16](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-16) — "In practice, if a motion to reconsider an affirmative vote on the Previous Question prevails, the vote that adopted the motion to Reconsider is also presumed to have carried out the reconsideration and to have reversed the vote that is reconsidered."
16. `[C0073 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:16](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-16) — "In practice, if a motion to reconsider an affirmative vote on the Previous Question prevails, the vote that adopted the motion to Reconsider is also presumed to have carried out the reconsideration and to have reversed the vote that is reconsidered."
17. `[C0075 · cloze]` Answer: **same**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-19) — "But when consideration is resumed at the same session—even on another day, as may happen in a convention—all such applicable orders remain in effect."
18. `[C0075 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:19](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-19) — "Except for the effect of an unexhausted order limiting or closing debate as just stated, when a question is taken up on a different day from the one on which it was postponed, the right of members to debate it begins over again, as if the question had not previously been debated;"
19. `[C0083 · cloze]` Answer: **adjourn**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-1) — "To adjourn means to close the meeting (8)."
20. `[C0083 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [21:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-21-1) — "To adjourn means to close the meeting (8)."
21. `[C0096 · cloze]` Answer: **Order of Business**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-11) — "It is not in order, either through a subsidiary motion or a main motion, to postpone a class of business composed of several items or subjects, such as reports of officers or reports of committees (see Order of Business, 41);"
22. `[C0096 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [14:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-14-11) — "It is not in order, either through a subsidiary motion or a main motion, to postpone a class of business composed of several items or subjects, such as reports of officers or reports of committees (see Order of Business, 41);"
23. `[C0125 · cloze]` Answer: **Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-23) — "If the assembly is not familiar with the use of the Previous Question, the chair should at this point explain it."
24. `[C0125 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-23) — "If the assembly is not familiar with the use of the Previous Question, the chair should at this point explain it."
25. `[C0126 · cloze]` Answer: **Commit**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:27](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-27) — "Assume that a resolution, an amendment to the resolution, and a motion to Commit are pending (in which case the motion to Commit is the immediately pending question)."
26. `[C0126 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [16:27](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-16-27) — "Assume that a resolution, an amendment to the resolution, and a motion to Commit are pending (in which case the motion to Commit is the immediately pending question)."
27. `[C0142 · cloze]` Answer: **Commit**. See RONR (12th ed.) [13:9](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-13-9) — "Dilatory Motion to Commit."

CHAIR: It is moved and seconded to amend by inserting in the primary amendment the word “landscaped” before “parking lot.” If the word is inserted, the primary amendment will be, “to add to the resolution for the purchase of the property, the words ‘and convert it into a landscaped parking lot.’” The question is on inserting the word “landscaped.”"

[15:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-15-14) — "If it is desired to order a limitation or extension of debate whose effect is other than as described above, this can be specified in the order, such as in Form and Example (e) below."
262. `[C1310 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [15:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-15-14) — "If it is desired to order a limitation or extension of debate whose effect is other than as described above, this can be specified in the order, such as in Form and Example (e) below."
263. `[C1318 · cloze]` Answer: **Postpone**. See RONR (12th ed.) 264. `[C1318 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) **Answer Key** (with Concept ID · format for SRS tracking)

1. `[C0002 · cloze]` Answer: **functioning of a society or assembly**. See RONR (12th ed.) [32:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-32-7) — "A request to be excused from a duty essential to the functioning of a society or assembly is a question of privilege affecting the organization of the assembly;"
2. `[C0002 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [32:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-32-7) — "A request to be excused from a duty essential to the functioning of a society or assembly is a question of privilege affecting the organization of the assembly;"
3. `[C0080 · cloze]` Answer: **Reconsider**. See RONR (12th ed.) [37:32](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-37-32) — "When a motion to Reconsider covers the votes on two or more connected motions, not all of these questions can be discussed in debate on the motion to Reconsider, but only the one that will be voted on first if the motion to Reconsider is adopted."
4. `[C0080 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [37:32](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-37-32) — "When a motion to Reconsider covers the votes on two or more connected motions, not all of these questions can be discussed in debate on the motion to Reconsider, but only the one that will be voted on first if the motion to Reconsider is adopted."
5. `[C0098 · cloze]` Answer: **Division**. See RONR (12th ed.) [30:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-30-1) — "The object of motions relating to methods of voting and the polls is to obtain a vote on a question in some form other than by voice, by show of hands, or by Division (rising);"
6. `[C0098 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [30:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-30-1) — "The object of motions relating to methods of voting and the polls is to obtain a vote on a question in some form other than by voice, by show of hands, or by Division (rising);"
7. `[C0110 · cloze]` Answer: **Previous Question**. See RONR (12th ed.) [25:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-25-11) — "Thus, while generally applicable limits on debate and the making of motions may be imposed by motions such as the Previous Question, the rules may not be suspended so as to deny any particular member the right to attend meetings, make motions or nominations, speak in debate, give previous notice, or vote."
8. `[C0110 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [25:11](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-25-11) — "Rules protecting a basic right of the individual member cannot be suspended."
9. `[C0115 · cloze]` Answer: **Reconsider**. See RONR (12th ed.) [37:37](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-37-37) — "If the maker of the motion to Reconsider fails to state which side he voted on, the chair, before making any other response, directs the member to do so:"
10. `[C0115 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [37:37](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-37-37) — "If the maker of the motion to Reconsider fails to state which side he voted on, the chair, before making any other response, directs the member to do so:"

17. `[C0151 · cloze]` Answer: **dispense with**. See RONR (12th ed.) [25:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-25-12) — "At a regular meeting of an organization that has an established order of business, the assembly cannot, even unanimously, vote to dispense with that order of business (in the sense of voting, in advance of the time when it adjourns, that the order of business shall not be gone through at all at that meeting)."
18. `[C0153 · cloze]` Answer: **Postpone Indefinitely**. See RONR (12th ed.) [35:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-35-4) — "In either of the situations described above, no subsidiary motion to Amend is in order that proposes a change going beyond the scope of the notice which was given, for the reason that adoption of such a motion will destroy the effect of the notice, and the motion is thus tantamount to a motion to Postpone Indefinitely."
19. `[C0153 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) 54. `[C0396 · cloze]` Answer: **Division**. See RONR (12th ed.) [29:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-29-7) — "When it is clear that there has been a full vote and there can be no reasonable doubt as to which side is in the majority, a call for a Division is dilatory, and the chair should not allow the individual member’s right of demanding a Division to be abused to the annoyance of the assembly."
55. `[C0396 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [29:7](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-29-7) — "When it is clear that there has been a full vote and there can be no reasonable doubt as to which side is in the majority, a call for a Division is dilatory, and the chair should not allow the individual member’s right of demanding a Division to be abused to the annoyance of the assembly."

## Domain 4: Organization and Conduct of Meetings

**1.** `[C0014 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: In general, for a member to speak when no question is pending, without promptly leading to a motion, implies an unusual circumstance and requires permission _____ assembly.

**2.** `[C0014 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: In general, for a member to speak when no question is pending, without promptly leading to a motion, implies an unusual circumstance and requires permission _____ assembly.

   A. of the
   B. Commit
   C. rules of order
   D. prevent consideration

**3.** `[C0072 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: In reference to an order of business specially adopted for a given session, the term program is often used instead of _____;

**4.** `[C0072 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: In reference to an order of business specially adopted for a given session, the term program is often used instead of _____;

   A. extend the limits
   B. agenda
   C. proxy
   D. strike out and insert

**5.** `[C0084 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: The usual wording then is, “I move the adoption of the following resolution: ‘_____, That…’”;

**6.** `[C0084 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: The usual wording then is, “I move the adoption of the following resolution: ‘_____, That…’”;

   A. revision
   B. Resolved
   C. assemblies
   D. Order Newly Revised

**7.** `[C0087 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: Matters that the bylaws require to be considered at a particular meeting, such as the nomination and election of officers, may be regarded as special orders for the meeting and be considered under the heading of _____ in the order of business.

**8.** `[C0087 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: Matters that the bylaws require to be considered at a particular meeting, such as the nomination and election of officers, may be regarded as special orders for the meeting and be considered under the heading of _____ in the order of business.

   A. Special Orders
   B. beyond
   C. Resolved,
   D. does

**9.** `[C0089 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: In the case of an adjournment, see _____ below.

**10.** `[C0089 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: In the case of an adjournment, see _____ below.

   A. Carrying Over Unfinished Business
   B. executive board,
   C. In Brief
   D. control of the assembly

**11.** `[C0099 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: If at any time the chair makes a mistake and assigns the floor to the wrong person when more than one member rose and addressed the chair promptly, a _____ can be raised.

**12.** `[C0099 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: If at any time the chair makes a mistake and assigns the floor to the wrong person when more than one member rose and addressed the chair promptly, a _____ can be raised.

   A. Point of Order
   B. recorder,
   C. Call of the House,
   D. legislative body

**13.** `[C0103 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is commonly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the general _____—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are.

**14.** `[C0103 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is commonly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the _____—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are.

   A. general parliamentary law
   B. limiting
   C. Reconsider and Enter on the Minutes
   D. strike out an entire paragraph

**15.** `[C0114 · cloze]` _Cloze recall_ — Fill in the blank: The application of the same principle to the case of _____ (which, as the term is understood in this book, do not deal with parliamentary procedure;

**16.** `[C0114 · term_mcq]` _Applied multiple-choice_ — Fill in the blank: The application of the same principle to the case of _____ (which, as the term is understood in this book, do not deal with parliamentary procedure;

   A. standing rules
   B. proposed to be reconsidered

**Answer Key** (with Concept ID · format for SRS tracking)

1. `[C0014 · cloze]` Answer: **of the**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:34](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-34) — "In general, for a member to speak when no question is pending, without promptly leading to a motion, implies an unusual circumstance and requires permission of the assembly."
2. `[C0014 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:34](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-34) — "In general, for a member to speak when no question is pending, without promptly leading to a motion, implies an unusual circumstance and requires permission of the assembly."
3. `[C0072 · cloze]` Answer: **agenda**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:64](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-64) — "In reference to an order of business specially adopted for a given session, the term program is often used instead of agenda;"
4. `[C0072 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:64](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-64) — "In reference to an order of business specially adopted for a given session, the term program is often used instead of agenda;"
5. `[C0084 · cloze]` Answer: **Resolved**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-4) — "The usual wording then is, “I move the adoption of the following resolution: ‘Resolved, That…’”;"
6. `[C0084 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-4) — "The usual wording then is, “I move the adoption of the following resolution: ‘Resolved, That…’”;"
7. `[C0087 · cloze]` Answer: **Special Orders**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:20](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-20) — "Matters that the bylaws require to be considered at a particular meeting, such as the nomination and election of officers, may be regarded as special orders for the meeting and be considered under the heading of Special Orders in the order of business."
8. `[C0087 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:20](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-20) — "Matters that the bylaws require to be considered at a particular meeting, such as the nomination and election of officers, may be regarded as special orders for the meeting and be considered under the heading of Special Orders in the order of business."
9. `[C0089 · cloze]` Answer: **Carrying Over Unfinished Business**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:68](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-68) — "In the case of an adjournment, see Carrying Over Unfinished Business below."
10. `[C0089 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:68](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-68) — "In the case of an adjournment, see Carrying Over Unfinished Business below."
11. `[C0099 · cloze]` Answer: **Point of Order**. See RONR (12th ed.) [42:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-42-15) — "If at any time the chair makes a mistake and assigns the floor to the wrong person when more than one member rose and addressed the chair promptly, a Point of Order can be raised."
12. `[C0099 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [42:15](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-42-15) — "If at any time the chair makes a mistake and assigns the floor to the wrong person when more than one member rose and addressed the chair promptly, a Point of Order can be raised."
13. `[C0103 · cloze]` Answer: **parliamentary law**. See RONR (12th ed.) [1:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-1-5) — "A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is commonly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the general parliamentary law—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are."
14. `[C0103 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [1:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-1-5) — "A deliberative assembly that has not adopted any rules is commonly understood to hold itself bound by the rules and customs of the general parliamentary law—or common parliamentary law (as discussed in the Introduction)—to the extent that there is agreement in the meeting body as to what these rules and practices are."
15. `[C0114 · cloze]` Answer: **standing rules**. See RONR (12th ed.) [8:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-8-13) — "The application of the same principle to the case of standing rules (which, as the term is understood in this book, do not deal with parliamentary procedure;"
16. `[C0114 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [8:13](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-8-13) — "The application of the same principle to the case of standing rules (which, as the term is understood in this book, do not deal with parliamentary procedure;"
17. `[C0118 · cloze]` Answer: **all**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-5) — "A member may both speak in debate and conclude by offering a secondary motion, which is a particular application of the principle that a member having been recognized for any legitimate purpose has the floor for all legitimate purposes."
18. `[C0118 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-5) — "A member may both speak in debate and conclude by offering a secondary motion, which is a particular application of the principle that a member having been recognized for any legitimate purpose has the floor for all legitimate purposes."
19. `[C0122 · cloze]` Answer: **disturb the assembly**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-28) — "During debate, during remarks by the presiding officer to the assembly, and during voting, no member should be permitted to disturb the assembly by whispering, walking across the floor, or in any other way."
20. `[C0122 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-28) — "During debate, during remarks by the presiding officer to the assembly, and during voting, no member should be permitted to disturb the assembly by whispering, walking across the floor, or in any other way."
21. `[C0178 · cloze]` Answer: **class**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:38](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-38) — "It is not in order to lay on the table or postpone a class of questions, like committee reports, or anything but the question that is actually before the assembly."
22. `[C0178 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:38](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-38) — "It is not in order to lay on the table or postpone a class of questions, like committee reports, or anything but the question that is actually before the assembly."
23. `[C0186 · cloze]` Answer: **not pending**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:44](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-44) — "When a question that is not pending is made an order of the day, it is usually made a special order."
24. `[C0186 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:44](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-44) — "It can be offered in this form: “I move that the following resolution be made a special order for the next meeting: ‘Resolved, That…’”;"
25. `[C0200 · cloze]` Answer: **chairman**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-5) — "The presiding officer of an assembly ordinarily is called the chairman when no special title has been assigned, or in a body not permanently organized, such as a mass meeting (53)."
26. `[C0200 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [47:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-47-5) — "The presiding officer of an assembly ordinarily is called the chairman when no special title has been assigned, or in a body not permanently organized, such as a mass meeting (53)."
27. `[C0211 · cloze]` Answer: **Reconsider**. See RONR (12th ed.) [42:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-42-12) — "When an undebatable motion that can be amended is reconsidered for that announced purpose, however, the maker of the motion to Reconsider (37) is entitled to preference in recognition, as explained in the preceding paragraph."
28. `[C0211 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [42:12](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-42-12) — "When an undebatable motion that can be amended is reconsidered for that announced purpose, however, the maker of the motion to Reconsider (37) is entitled to preference in recognition, as explained in the preceding paragraph."

264. `[C1393 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [3:21](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-3-21) — "Business is brought before an assembly by the motion of a member."
265. `[C1406 · cloze]` Answer: **Appeal**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:39](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-39) — "In the case of an Appeal that relates to indecorum, the rules of debate, or the priority of business, it is assumed that debate would be a hindrance to business, as it would be if the appeal were made when an undebatable question is immediately pending or involved in the appeal."
266. `[C1406 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:39](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-39) — "A Request to Be Excused from a Duty, such as a resignation, may require some discussion for its proper decision, and for this reason it is debatable."
267. `[C1412 · cloze]` Answer: **adopted**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:46](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-46) — "The form of the third point—which is usually needed only for a vote that has caused a motion to be adopted—is determined by the particular motion."
268. `[C1412 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:46](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-46) — "The form of the third point—which is usually needed only for a vote that has caused a motion to be adopted—is determined by the particular motion."
269. `[C1420 · cloze]` Answer: **deliberative**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-1) — "In a deliberative assembly, this term applies to discussion on the merits of a pending question—that is, whether the proposal under consideration should, or should not, be agreed to."
270. `[C1420 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [43:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-43-1) — "Debate, rightly understood, is an essential element in the making of rational decisions of consequence by intelligent people."
271. `[C1422 · cloze]` Answer: **Unfinished Business and General Orders**. See RONR (12th ed.) [41:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-41-23) — "The heading of Unfinished Business and General Orders includes items of business in the four categories that are listed below in the order in which they are taken up."

273. `[C1428 · cloze]` Answer: **aye**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:37](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-37) — "Those in favor of the motion, say aye."
274. `[C1428 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [4:37](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-4-37) — "Those in favor of the motion, say aye."
275. `[C1430 · cloze]` Answer: **secretary**. See RONR (12th ed.) [3:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-3-6) — "The minimum essential officers for the conduct of business in a deliberative assembly are a presiding officer, who conducts the meeting and sees that the rules are observed, and a secretary, or clerk, who makes a written record of what is done—usually called “the minutes.” If the officers are members of the assembly—as they usually are in ordinary societies—they are counted in determining whether a quorum is present."
276. `[C1430 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [3:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-3-6) — "The minimum essential officers for the conduct of business in a deliberative assembly are a presiding officer, who conducts the meeting and sees that the rules are observed, and a secretary, or clerk, who makes a written record of what is done—usually called “the minutes.” If the officers are members of the assembly—as they usually are in ordinary societies—they are counted in determining whether a quorum is present."

278. `[C1445 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) **Answer Key** (with Concept ID · format for SRS tracking)

1. `[C0003 · cloze]` Answer: **sine die**. See RONR (12th ed.) [50:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-50-23) — "When a special committee has finished with the business assigned to it, a motion is made for the committee to “rise”—which is equivalent to the motion to adjourn sine die (or without day)—and for the chairman or some other member to make its report to the assembly."
2. `[C0003 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [50:23](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-50-23) — "When a special committee has finished with the business assigned to it, a motion is made for the committee to “rise”—which is equivalent to the motion to adjourn sine die (or without day)—and for the chairman or some other member to make its report to the assembly."
3. `[C0007 · cloze]` Answer: **action,**. See RONR (12th ed.) [51:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-51-4) — "Although it is possible for a report, in the circumstances just described, to present recommendations which are not in the form of resolutions or motions, the “adoption” of such recommendations by the parent assembly may, depending on their wording or that of the motion to adopt, lead to confusion as to whether their adoption authorizes action, or only has the force of a declaration of intent (requiring the adoption of subsequent resolutions for implementation)."
4. `[C0007 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [51:4](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-51-4) — "Although it is possible for a report, in the circumstances just described, to present recommendations which are not in the form of resolutions or motions, the “adoption” of such recommendations by the parent assembly may, depending on their wording or that of the motion to adopt, lead to confusion as to whether their adoption authorizes action, or only has the force of a declaration of intent (requiring the adoption of subsequent resolutions for implementation)."
5. `[C0046 · cloze]` Answer: **order of business**. See RONR (12th ed.) [59:48](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-59-48) — "When the program is adopted by the voting body, with or without amendment, it becomes the order of business of the entire convention session (41)."
6. `[C0046 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [59:48](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-59-48) — "When the program is adopted by the voting body, with or without amendment, it becomes the order of business of the entire convention session (41)."
7. `[C0048 · cloze]` Answer: **revision**. See RONR (12th ed.) [57:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-57-5) — "Changes of the bylaws that are so extensive and general that they are scattered throughout the bylaws should be effected through the substitution of an entirely new set of bylaws, called a revision."
8. `[C0048 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [57:5](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-57-5) — "Changes of the bylaws that are so extensive and general that they are scattered throughout the bylaws should be effected through the substitution of an entirely new set of bylaws, called a revision."
9. `[C0052 · cloze]` Answer: **Resolved,**. See RONR (12th ed.) [55:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-55-6) — "In the case of an unincorporated society, a resolution should be prepared, such as: “Resolved, That the X Society be dissolved as of March 31, 20.” This resolution may be preceded by a preamble setting forth the reasons for the dissolution."
10. `[C0052 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [55:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-55-6) — "In the case of an unincorporated society, a resolution should be prepared, such as: “Resolved, That the X Society be dissolved as of March 31, 20.” This resolution may be preceded by a preamble setting forth the reasons for the dissolution."
11. `[C0090 · cloze]` Answer: **society,**. See RONR (12th ed.) [49:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-49-14) — "In such cases the committees are genuinely subordinate to the board and must ordinarily report back to it for authority to act (in contrast to an executive committee, which usually has power to act as the board, and in contrast to standing committees of the society, which are not subordinate to the board unless made so by a provision in the bylaws)."
12. `[C0090 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [49:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-49-14) — "In such cases the committees are genuinely subordinate to the board and must ordinarily report back to it for authority to act (in contrast to an executive committee, which usually has power to act as the board, and in contrast to standing committees of the society, which are not subordinate to the board unless made so by a provision in the bylaws)."
13. `[C0094 · cloze]` Answer: **adopt, accept,**. See RONR (12th ed.) [51:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-51-14) — "As applied to an assembly’s action with respect to board or committee reports or any of their contents, the expressions adopt, accept, and agree to are all equivalent—that is, the text adopted becomes in effect the act or statement of the assembly."
14. `[C0094 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **D**. See RONR (12th ed.) [51:14](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-51-14) — "As applied to an assembly’s action with respect to board or committee reports or any of their contents, the expressions adopt, accept, and agree to are all equivalent—that is, the text adopted becomes in effect the act or statement of the assembly."
15. `[C0138 · cloze]` Answer: **Reconsider,**. See RONR (12th ed.) [57:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-57-6) — "An affirmative vote adopting such an arrangement is not subject to a motion to Reconsider, nor may a later, separate amendment be offered as a substitute for a pending one."
16. `[C0138 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [57:6](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-57-6) — "An affirmative vote adopting such an arrangement is not subject to a motion to Reconsider, nor may a later, separate amendment be offered as a substitute for a pending one."
17. `[C0204 · cloze]` Answer: **Recess**. See RONR (12th ed.) [52:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-52-28) — "The more traditional aids to the crystallization of opinion in societies have been, simply, to take a Recess or to refer the matter to a committee—often a large committee composed of members representing differing views in the society, such as a committee of the whole or one of its alternate forms."
18. `[C0204 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **C**. See RONR (12th ed.) [52:28](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-52-28) — "The more traditional aids to the crystallization of opinion in societies have been, simply, to take a Recess or to refer the matter to a committee—often a large committee composed of members representing differing views in the society, such as a committee of the whole or one of its alternate forms."
19. `[C0209 · cloze]` Answer: **by article or section**. See RONR (12th ed.) [54:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-54-17) — "Since a complete set of bylaws is commonly considered by article or section (see 28), the chair states the question as follows:"
20. `[C0209 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **B**. See RONR (12th ed.) [54:17](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-54-17) — "Since a complete set of bylaws is commonly considered by article or section (see 28), the chair states the question as follows:"
21. `[C0256 · cloze]` Answer: **order of business**. See RONR (12th ed.) [59:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-59-3) — "and (3) the Program Committee, which works out a convention program combining a suitable order of business (41) with special features designed to promote and develop the association or society as a whole."
22. `[C0256 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [59:3](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-59-3) — "and (3) the Program Committee, which works out a convention program combining a suitable order of business (41) with special features designed to promote and develop the association or society as a whole."
23. `[C0303 · cloze]` Answer: **adding**. See RONR (12th ed.) [51:51](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-51-51) — "but if the motion to substitute is adopted, the resolution thus substituted can be amended only by adding."

[58:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-58-1) — "As commonly understood in parliamentary law and as used in this book, the word convention refers to an assembly of delegates (other than a permanently constituted public lawmaking body), who are usually chosen specially for each session as representatives of the constituent units or subdivisions within a larger group of people, to sit as a single deliberative body acting in the name of the entire group."
99. `[C1478 · term_mcq]` Correct answer: **A**. See RONR (12th ed.) [58:1](roberts_rules_of_order_12th_edition.md#p-58-1) — "Other terms by which such a convention may be described in some organizations include congress, conference, convocation, general assembly, house of delegates, and house of representatives."
